(4)  In  the  case  falling  under  subparagraphs  1  and  2-2(a)  of  paragraph  (1)  and 
subparagraphs 1(g) and 2(a) (referring to the cases falling under subparagraph 1(g) of the 
same paragraph) of paragraph (2), the relevant quotation shall not be inputted until the 
opening price is determined and notified. [May 7, 2021] (Amended on April 12, 2023) 

§15. Conversion of Limit-to-market-on-close Quotations 

(1) Limit-to-market-on-close quotations shall be deemed, in accordance with [§12(2)] of 
the  Regulation,  to  have  been  converted  into  the  market  quotations  according  to  the 
following priority:   

1. Lower price offer quotation shall have priority over the higher price offer quotations 
and higher price bid quotation shall have priority over the lower price bid quotations; 
and   

2. In case of same price quotations, the priority shall be assigned according to the time 
when the quotations are received, thus the quotation received earlier having priority 
over the ones received later.   

(2)  In  cases  where  a  limit-to-market-on-close  quotation  is  converted  into  a  market 
quotation pursuant to paragraph (1), the converted market quotation shall be deemed to 
have  been  received  at  the  opening  time  of  quotation  receiving  hours  pursuant  to  the 
forepart of the main sentence of [§35(1)3]. Provided that it shall be deemed to have been 
received at the relevant resuming time in the case of the latter part of the main sentence 
of [§35(1)3], and it shall be deemed to have been received ten (10) minutes before the 
market closing in the case of the proviso to [§35(1)4]. (Amended on May 19; December 
22, 2022) 

§15-2.  Priority  of  Occurrence  of  Validity  from  Stop-limit  Quotation  to  Limit 
Quotation 

(1)  Pursuant  to  [§12(2)]  of  the  Regulation,  the  priority  of  occurrence  of  validity  from 
stop-limit quotations to limit quotations shall be as follows: 

    1. In stop-limit  sell quotations, a stop-limit  quotation  with  a higher  stop  price takes 

precedence over a stop-limit quotation with a lower stop price; 

    2.  In  stop-limit  buy  quotations,  a  stop-limit  quotation  with  a  lower  stop  price  takes 

precedence over a stop-limit quotation with a higher stop price; and 

    3. In cases where stop prices are the same, the stop-limit quotation received first takes 
precedence over the stop-limit quotation received later, based on the time the stop-limit 
quotation was received. 

(2) In applying [§22(2)2] of the Regulation to the stop-limit quotation whose validity as 
a limit quotation is triggered pursuant to paragraph (1), the time at which the stop-limit 

39 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
quotation triggers into a limit quotation shall be deemed as the time of receiving the stop-
limit quotation. 

[February 27, 2025] 

§16. Conversion Method between Quotation Price and Yield of Debt Securities 

The Exchange may, pursuant to [§12(2)] of the Regulation, convert the quotation prices 
and yields of debt securities by the following methods and disclose them. In such cases, 
the numbers after the fourth decimal place shall be discarded: (Amended on February 3, 
2009; February 28, 2014) 

1. Discount bonds and compound interest bonds   

(a) Odd period less than a year: By simple discount method; and   

(b) Period per annum: By compound discount method.   

2. Coupon bonds   

(a) Period less than a unit interest payment period: By simple discount method; and   

(b) Unit interest payment period: By compound discount method.   

§17. Cancellation and Correction of Quotations 

(1) Members may, pursuant to [§13(2)] of the Regulation, cancel or correct all or a part 
of the quoted quantity. Provided that the cancellation of a part of quotation for auction-
based block trade shall be allowed only in cases where the quotation quantity remaining 
after the cancellation satisfies the quantity requirement pursuant to [§48-2(3) and §51-
3(3)]. (Amended on March 19, 2009; July 29, 2010) 

(2)  Members  may,  pursuant  to  [§13(2)]  of  the  Regulation,  correct  the  quotations 
according to any of the following methods: (Amended on March 19, 2009; July 11, 2019) 

1. In cases where a limit quotation, limit-to-market-on-close quotation, immediately 
executable limit  quotation  or best  limit  quotation  is  corrected into the same type of 
quotation, all or a part of quoted quantity may be corrected using a different price. In 
such cases, in case of an immediately executable limit quotation or best limit quotation, 
it shall refer to the case where the price before the correction is different from the price 
after the correction; and 

1-2. In cases of correcting a stop-limit quotation to a quotation of the same type, all or 
part of the quantity of the quotation shall be corrected using any one method of the 
following items: [February 27, 2025] 

        (a) If a stop-limit quotation is corrected before it triggers into a limit quotation, either 

40 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
the price of quotation before the correction shall be different from the price of the 
quotation after the correction, or the stop price before the correction shall be different 
from the stop price after the correction; or [February 27, 2025] 

        (b) If a stop-limit quotation is corrected after it triggers into a limit quotation, the 

price of the quotation shall be different. [February 27, 2025] 

2.  In  cases  where  a  limit  quotation,  market  quotation,  limit-to-market-on-close 
quotation, immediately executable limit quotation or best limit quotation is corrected 
into  a  different  type  of  quotation  (mid-price  quotation  and  stop-limit  quotation  are 
excluded; the same hereinafter in this subparagraph), whole or a part of quoted quantity 
may  be  corrected  into  a  different  type  of  quotation.  Provided  that,  as  a  case  falling 
under any of the following items, it shall exclude the case where the price before the 
correction is the same as the price after the correction. (Amended on February 27, 2025) 

(a) Case of correcting a limit quotation to an immediately executable limit quotation 
or best limit quotation; 

(b) Case of correcting an immediately executable limit quotation to a limit quotation 
or best limit quotation; and 

(c)  Case  of  correcting  a  best  limit  quotation  to  a  limit  quotation  or  immediately 
executable limit quotation. 

(3) In the case of correction of quotations pursuant to paragraph (2), such correction shall 
be valid from the time of receiving such corrected quotation. (Amended on March 19, 
2009) 

§17-2. Mass Order Cancellation 

(1)  Members  may  apply  to  the  Exchange  to  cancel  all  quotations  received  before 
application  at  once  (hereinafter  referred  to  as  the  “mass  order  cancellation”)  by 
designating conditions for each high-speed algorithmic trading number only if all of the 
following subparagraphs are met. In such case, matters necessary for the application of 
the  mass  order  cancellation,  such  as  classification  of  securities,  conditions  for 
cancellation, etc. shall be as specified in the Annex 1-3: 

1.  Cases for managing risks; and 

2.  Cases  for  submitting  quotations  through  high-speed  algorithmic  trading  account 

reported pursuant to [§104-3(3)] of the Regulation. 

(2)  Notwithstanding  paragraph  (1),  the  Exchange  may  not  process  the  mass  order 
cancellation in case of a system failure or other cases when it is deemed necessary for 
market management.   

(3) Members shall record and maintain data related to the mass order cancellation for ten 

41 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
(10) years and submit the data when the Exchange request for the relevant data for market 
management, etc. 

[December 22, 2022] 

§17-3. Methods to Apply for Cancellation of Disconnected Quotations, etc. 

(1)  The  “case  where  it  is  stipulated  in  the  Enforcement  Rules”  in  [§13-2(1)]  of  the 
Regulation shall refer to the case where, as a case in which the connection between the 
member  system  and  the  Exchange  system  is  disconnected  during  the  regular  trading 
session and electronic transmission and reception does not occur, there is a determination 
in advance between the member applying for the cancellation of disconnected quotations 
and the Exchange.     

(2) Pursuant to [§13-2(1)] of the Regulation, the range of cancellation of disconnected 
quotations shall be the number (excluding the number changed or cancelled through other 
sessions)  of  quotations  not  executed  among  quotations  submitted  through  the  session 
requested in advance pursuant to paragraph (4).   

(3) Pursuant to [§13-2(2)] of the Regulation, trades of debt securities shall be excluded 
from the application for the cancellation of disconnected quotations.   

(4) Pursuant to [§13-2(2)] of the Regulation, the methods to apply for the cancellation of 
disconnected quotations and for the termination thereof shall be as specified in [§8(5)] of 
the Guidelines for Connection, etc. of Member System. 

(5) The Exchange may not apply the cancellation of disconnection quotations in case of 
system failure or other cases where it deems necessary for market management. 

[December 22, 2022] 

§18. Records of Quotations 

(1) Pursuant to [§14(2)] of the Regulation, the record of quotations shall be kept in the 
order book in accordance with [Annex: Form No. 2].   

(2) The total quantity per price, upon specifying the bid or offer, shall be recorded in the 
order book pursuant to paragraph (1). 

CHAPTER III.TRADING OF STOCKS, ETC. 

Section 1. Common Provisions 

42 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
§19. Scope of Application 

This  Chapter  shall  apply  to  the  trading  of  stocks,  DRs  of  foreign  stocks,  collective 
investment securities of ETFs, ETNs, subscription right certificates, subscription warrants, 
ELWs  and  beneficiary  certificates.  (Amended  on  February  3,  2009;  July  16,  2009; 
September 2, 2014))   

Section 2. Administration of Quotations and Price Limit 

§20. Prior Notice on Suspension of Validity of Program Trading Quotations, etc. 

(1) The Exchange may, when the price of the contract whose trading volume is the largest 
pursuant to [§16(1)] of the Regulation (hereinafter in this Article referred to as “the base 
contract”) rise (or fall) 5/100 or more over (or below) the base price, issue a prior notice 
about the fact that the validity of bid (or offer) quotations for program trading may be 
suspended. (Amended on February 3, 2009) 

(2) The Exchange may call off the prior notice on the suspension of quotation validity in 
cases where the price of base contract drops within 5/100 of the base price after issuing 
the prior notice under paragraph (1) or in cases where the trading of the base contract is 
halted pursuant to [§76] of the Derivatives Market Business Regulation. (Amended on 
February 3, 2009) 

(3) Notwithstanding paragraphs (1) and (2), when a temporary failure of the Exchange 
computer  system  occurs,  the  Exchange  may  not  issue  or  call  off  a  prior  notice  on  the 
suspension of validity of program trading quotation. (Amended on February 3, 2009) 

§21. [Deleted on December 6, 2018] 

§22. [Deleted on December 6, 2018] 

§23. [Deleted on February 3, 2009] 

§24. [Deleted on February 3, 2009] 

§24-2. Methods of Verifying Covered Short Sale 

(1) The “manner stipulated in the Enforcement Rules” in [§17(3)3] of the Regulation shall 
refer to the preservation of the documents, tape recordings or electronic storage devices 
that validate the date and details of orders, which the member received from a customer, 
for a period of longer than three (3) years that is determined by the member. 

(2) [Deleted on February 28, 2017] 

[March 6, 2009] 

43 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
§24-3. Restrictions of Quotations for Covered Short Sale 

(1)  The  “covered  short  sale  quotations  placed  to  conduct  the  trades  stipulated  in  the 
Enforcement Rules” in the proviso to the part other than subparagraphs of [§17(6)] of the 
Regulation shall refer to any of the following subparagraphs: (Amended on March 12, 
2021) 

1.  Quotations  falling  under  any  of  subparagraphs  6  through  8  of  [§18(2)]  of  the 
Regulation;   

2. Liquidity providing quotations pursuant to [§20-2(1)] of the Regulation and market-
making quotations pursuant to [§20-9(1)] of the Regulation; and 

3. Other quotations placed for the trades that the Exchange deems necessary. 

(2) The “issues falling under the criteria set forth in the Enforcement Rules” in [§17(6)1] 
of the Regulation shall refer to the issues that fall under any of the following requirements 
(limited to the stock certificates and the DRs of foreign stocks, and hereinafter referred to 
as the “overheated short sale issues”). (Amended on September 7, 2017; August 26, 2022; 
April 12, 2023; February 27, 2025) 

1. Issues of which the stock price decline rate, the proportion of short sale trading value 
to the market, and the increase rate of short sale trading value meet all of the following 
Items: 

(a)  The closing price of the day shall not less than 90/100 and not more than 95/100 

of the base price of the day; 

(b) The proportion of the trading value of covered short sale to the trading value of 
the day shall be at least three (3) times (if the value is greater than 20%, it shall 
be set at 20%) the proportion of the trading value of covered short sale (numbers 
shall  be  rounded  off  to  the  third  decimal  point)  for  the  quarter  immediately 
preceding the quarter in which the relevant trading day falls to the total trading 
value of listed stocks (limited to stocks and DRs of foreign stocks) for the same 
period; and 

(c)  The trading value of covered short sale of the day shall be at least six (6) times 
the average of the trading value of covered short sale for the latest forty (40) 
trading days. 

2. Issues of which the price decline rate and the increase rate of short sale trading value 
meet all of the following Items: 

    (a) The closing price of the day shall be 90/100 or lower of the base price of the day;   

and 

44 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
    (b) The increase rate in Subparagraph 1(c) shall be satisfied. 

3. Issues of which the price decline rate and the proportion and the increase rate of the 
trading value of covered short sale meet all of the following Items: 

(a)  The closing price of the day shall be 97/100 or lower of the base price of the day; 

(b) The proportion of trading value of covered short sale to trading value of the day 

is 30% or more; and (Amended on February 27, 2025) 

        (c) The trading value of covered short sale of the day shall be at least two (2) times 
the average of the trading  value of covered short sale for the latest  forty  (40) 
trading days. 

(3) The “trading value of covered short sale”, “trading value of the day”, and “trading 
value of listed stocks (limited to stocks and DRs of foreign stocks)” in each subparagraph 
of  paragraph  (2)  shall  be  calculated  by  including  each  trading  value  (limited  to  each 
trading  value  during  trading  hours  when  covered  short  sale  is  possible;  the  same 
hereinafter in the paragraph) of multilateral trading companies. Provided that, in cases 
where the Exchange cannot receive information on each trading value from a multilateral 
trading company due to system failure, etc., such information may be excluded from the 
calculation. [February 27, 2025] 

(4)  Notwithstanding  paragraphs  (2)  and  (3),  stocks  falling  under  each  of  following 
subparagraphs  shall  be  excluded  from  the  overheated  short  sale  issues:  [February  27, 
2025] 

    1. Issues using the first trading price as the base price; and [February 27, 2025] 

    2. Newly listed issues noted in [§30(1)2(a)];. [February 27, 2025] 

    3. Issues for which trading is not  established during the regular market hours of the 
Exchange or the multilateral trading company within the regular market hours of the 
Exchange. In this case, if the trading information of the multilateral trading company 
cannot  be  received  due  to  system  failure,  etc.,  the  establishment  of  trading  at  the 
multilateral trading company may not be taken into consideration; [February 27, 2025] 

    4. Issues scheduled to be delisted; [February 27, 2025] 

    5. Issues for which the number of trading days with executed trades during each trading 
hour, where covered short sale is possible during trading hours of the Exchange and 
multilateral trading companies, is less than twenty (20) days within the latest forty (40) 
trading  days.  In  this  case,  if  transaction  information  from  the  multilateral  trading 
company cannot be received due to system failure, etc., the day on which trading was 
established at the multilateral trading company may not be taken into consideration. 
[February 27, 2025] 

45 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
(5) The Exchange may officially announce the overheated short sale issues specified in 
paragraph (2) and restrict the quotations for covered short sale for one (1) day of the next 
trading day. Provided that, if the closing price of the relevant issue on the day when the 
restriction of covered short sale quotation is terminated is 95/100 or less of the base price 
of the day, the restriction of covered short sale quotation shall be extended until the next 
trading day and applied repeatedly at the end of every extension period. (Amended on 
August 26, 2022) (Moved from Paragraph (4), previous Paragraph (3) deleted on August 
26, 2022) 

(6) Notwithstanding paragraphs (2) through (5), if deemed necessary for the purposes of 
market management due to drastic changes in market conditions etc., the Exchange may 
set differently the criteria for overheated short sale issues under paragraph (2) and adjust 
the  period  of  restrictions  on  quotations  for  covered  short  sales  under  paragraph  (5). 
[March 9, 2020] (Amended on August 26, 2022; February 27, 2025)   

(Wholly amended on February 28, 2017) 

§25. Restriction of Quotation price for Covered Short Sales 

(1) Pursuant to [§18(3)] of the Regulation, the proviso to [§18(1)] of the Regulation shall 
not  apply  to  the  case  falling  under  any  of  the  following  subparagraphs:  (Amended  on 
August 28, 2007; February 3, 2009) 

1. Case where the opening price is not yet determined; and   

2. When the opening price is the same as the most recent price (it shall be the closing 
price of the most recent trading day, but, if there exists the base price, it shall be the 
base price), the case where no price that is different from the relevant price has been 
determined.   

(2) [Deleted on August 28, 2007]   

(3) The provisions of [§18(1)] of the Regulation shall not  apply to the regular session 
auction-based block trade, regular session block trading, regular session basket trading 
and off-hours trading (excluding the off-hours call auction). (Amended on May 13, 2005; 
February 3, 2009; July 29, 2010)   

§25-2. Arbitrage Trading of Index, etc. 

(1) “A trade that is stipulated in the Enforcement Rules” in [§18(2)1] of the Regulation 
shall  refer  to  a  trade  falling  under  any  of  the  following  subparagraphs:  (Amended  on 
December 28, 2018; March 12, 2021) 

1.  An index arbitrage trade under [§2(21)1] of the Regulation; 

2. A trade where the sale (including the final settlement of a buying contract) of index 

46 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
futures  based  on  sector  index  is  conducted  at  the  same  time  or  immediately 
before/after the purchase of the basket of stocks linked to the sector index; and 

3. A trade where the purchase (including the final settlement of a selling contract) of 
index  futures  based  on  sector  index  is  conducted  at  the  same  time  or  immediately 
before/after the sales of the basket of stocks linked to the sector index.   

(2) The provisions of [§6-4(4)] shall apply mutatis mutandis to the case of the sale or the 
purchase under paragraph (1). (Amended on December 28, 2018) 

[December 10, 2014] 

§26. Stock Arbitrage Trading 

(1) “A trade that is stipulated in the Enforcement Rules” in [§18(2)2] of the Regulation 
shall  refer  to  a  trade  falling  under  any  of  the  following  subparagraphs:  (Amended  on 
December 27, 2007; December 28, 2018) 

1. A trade where the sale (including the final settlement of a buying contract) of single 
stock futures (including the synthetic stock futures) based on the relevant underlying 
stocks  is  conducted  at  the  same  time  or  immediately  after/before  the  purchase  of 
underlying stocks; and   

2. A trade where the purchase (including the final settlement of a selling contract) of 
single  stock  futures  (including  the  synthetic  stock  futures)  based  on  the  relevant 
underlying stocks is conducted at the same time or immediately after/before the sale of 
underlying stocks.   

(2)  The  “sale  of  synthetic  stock  futures”  mentioned  in  paragraph  (1)  shall  refer  to  the 
purchase of a put option while selling a call option, and the "purchase of synthetic stock 
futures" shall refer to the sale of a put option while buying a call option. (Amended on 
December 28, 2018) 

(3) The provisions of [§6-4(4)] shall apply mutatis mutandis to the case of the purchase 
or sale under paragraph (1).   

§27. [Deleted on March 12, 2021] 

§27-2. [Deleted on March 12, 2021] 

§28. DR Arbitrage Trading 

(1) “A trade that is stipulated in the Enforcement Rules” in [§18(2)4] of the Regulation 
shall  refer  to  a  trade  falling  under  any  of  the  following  subparagraphs:  (Amended  on 
February 3, 2009) 

1. A trade where the sale of the underlying stocks is conducted simultaneously with or 

47 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
immediately after/before the purchase of DRs (including the DRs for foreign stocks: 
the same hereinafter in this Article); and   

2. A trade where the purchase of the underlying stocks is  conducted simultaneously 
with or immediately after/before the sale of DRs.   

(2) The provisions of [§6-4(4)] shall apply mutatis mutandis to the case of the purchase 
or sale under paragraph (1). (Amended on February 3, 2009; December 28, 2018) 

§28-2. Follow-up Management of Short Sale Quotations 

(1) Each member shall preserve the records and relevant materials pursuant to [§18-2(1)] 
of the Regulation for the period determined by the member, which is longer than three (3) 
years.   

(2) In verifying the balance of securities held and the quantity of securities to be settled 
pursuant to [§18-2(1)] of the Regulation, if the customer has electronically registered the 
relevant  securities  through  trust  companies  or  depository  institutions,  members  shall 
obtain a notification on the status of settlement shortage from the trust companies or the 
depository institutions in accordance with [Annex: Form No. 2-2], by 12:00 noon on the 
settlement date. In such cases, if a trust company or a depository institution notifies the 
customer of the information on settlement shortage via the information network of the 
Korea Securities Depository (hereinafter referred to as “KSD”) (limited to the case where 
reasons  for the settlement failure  are stated  according to the classifications in [Annex: 
Form No. 2-2]), it shall be deemed that such notification has been made in accordance 
with  [Annex:  Form No.  2-2]. (Amended on September 20, 2012,  December 18, 2013; 
September 10, 2019) 

(3) “The latest six (6) months” in the part other than each subparagraph of [§18-2(3)] of 
the Regulation shall be calculated by counting from the day when the Exchange verified 
the fact that the customer had sold the securities not in possession or the securities that 
cannot be settled by the settlement date. (Amended on September 20, 2012) 

(4) When the entire selling securities are collected as the entrustment guarantee money 
during the 120-day period from the trading day following the settlement date pursuant to 
[§89(1)2], each item under [§18-2(3)] of the Regulation shall not apply. [December 18, 
2013] (Amended on December 28, 2018) 

[March 6, 2009] 

§29. [Deleted on December 1, 2005] 

§30. Base Prices 

(1) The base prices of stocks, DRs of foreign stocks, collective investment securities of 
ETFs,  exchange-traded  notes  and  beneficiary  certificates  pursuant  to  [§20(1)]  of  the 
Regulation, shall be the prices under each of the following subparagraph: (Amended on 

48 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
August 26, 2005; February 3, 2009; July 16, 2009; January 27, 2011; December 28, 2011; 
April 20, 2012; May 12, 2014; December 10, 2014; September 10, 2019; June 23, 2020; 
July 23, 2020; February 14, 2022; April 12, 2023) 

1. In the case of issues other than those mentioned in  subparagraphs 2 through 6, it 
shall be the closing price of the previous day (if this price does not match the quotation 
price unit, it shall be the price closest to that price among the prices that are higher than 
that price and match the quotation price unit, and if the closing price of the previous 
day is not available, the base price of previous day; the same hereinafter); (Amended 
on February 27, 2025) 

2. The base prices of initially listed issues shall be as follows:   

(a) For stocks and DRs of foreign stocks: The price calculated according to [Annex                 
1-4]   

(b) For stocks transferred from the KOSDAQ Market: The closing price of the last 
trading day in the KOSDAQ Market. Provided that, if no closing price is available, 
the base price of the relevant trading day.   

(c) For collective investment securities of ETFs and beneficiary certificates noted in 
Article 189 of the Act: The base price calculated pursuant to Article 238(6) of the 
Act. In this case, it shall be the most recently announced base price as of the listing 
date, and if the announcement takes place on the day before the listing date, it shall 
be limited to the price announced by 17:00 hours.   

(d) For ETNs: The indicative value per share calculated pursuant to [§149-3(2)4] of 
the KOSPI Market Listing Regulation.   

(e) For beneficiary certificates other than beneficiary certificates under item (c): The 
public offering price at the recent initial public offering (excluding cases deemed as 
an initial public offering pursuant to Article 11(2) of the Enforcement Decree of the 
Act; the same hereinafter) or the secondary distribution.   

3. The base price of an issue using the first trading price as the base price shall be the 
first price determined in accordance with [§37(1)] of the Regulation. In this case, if the 
first price is not determined by the time of market closing, the lowest offer price if the 
offer prices which are lower than the appraisal price [in case of no appraisal price, the 
lowest quotation price shall be regarded as the appraisal price, and in the case of an 
issue using the first trading price as the base price noted in Subparagraph 3(b) of [§2], 
the price (if the relevant price is not positive, the lowest price among quotation price 
units) obtained by subtracting the amount of distribution or dividend per share from 
the closing price on the day before the two (2) trading day from the record date noted 
in [§132(1)] shall be regarded as the appraisal price; the same hereinafter and [§36]] 
determined  according  to  [Annex  1]  (the  lowest  quotation  price  shall  be  deemed  the 
appraisal price in case the appraisal price is not available; the same hereinafter in this 
Article and [§36]) are available, the highest bid price if the bid prices which are higher 

49 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
than the appraisal price are available, and the appraisal price in any other cases shall 
be the base price of the next trading day, respectively. 

3-2. In the case of issues listed after a merger, the base price shall be as follows: 

(a)  In the case where the special purpose acquisition company survives the merger 
pursuant to [§2(1)1(d)(i)] of the KOSPI Market Listing Regulation: 

The base price shall be the stock price under subparagraph 1 of the surviving special 
purpose acquisition company. 

(b)  In the case where the special purpose acquisition company does not survive the 
merger pursuant to [§2(1)1(d)(ii)] of the KOSPI Market Listing Regulation: 

The  base  price  shall  be  the  price  obtained  by  dividing  the  stock  price  under 
subparagraph  1  of  the  non-surviving  special  purpose  acquisition  company  by  the 
merger ratio (the number of new shares issued per share of the non-surviving special 
purpose acquisition company) of the corporation that is the counterpart to the merger 
in the report on completion of merger, etc. or the report on the issuance of securities 
submitted in connection with the merger. 

4. For the issues falling under any of the following items, from among the issues that 
have undergone ex-dividends or ex-rights, the base prices shall be the prices calculated 
according to the formulas in [Annex 2]. In the case of an issue to which such formulas 
cannot apply, from among the formulas under [Annex 2], the formula applicable to the 
issue most similar to the relevant issue shall be used.   

(a) Issues undergone ex-dividends following a prior notice for stock dividend for the 
relevant business year;   

(b) Issues undergone ex-rights following the capital increase without consideration; 
and   

(c)  Issue  undergone  ex-rights  following  the  capital  increase  with  consideration 
where the closing price of the day before ex-rights is higher than the issuing price of 
new shares.   

4-2. [Deleted on April 12, 2023] 

5. In the case of stocks of collective investment securities of ETFs or  ETNs, which 
have reported the cash distribution to the Exchange, the base price shall be the price 
obtained by subtracting amount of cash distribution per share (or per unit) (in case the 
distributable amount is not determined, it shall be the estimated distribution amount 
determined by taking into account the base price calculated pursuant to Article 238(6) 
of the Act,  which was  published by 17:00 hours) from  the closing price on two (2) 
trading days before the record day pursuant to [§132(1)];   

50 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
5-2. [Deleted on December 10] 

6. For issues undergone a stock split or a reverse stock split, the base price shall be the 
price obtained by multiplying the closing price of the previous day by the ratio of such 
split or reverse split;         

6-2. [Deleted on April 12, 2023] 

7. [Deleted on April 12, 2023]   

8. [Deleted on April 12, 2023] 

9. [Deleted on April 12, 2023]   

(2) [Deleted on April 12, 2023] 

(3) In cases where the price under subparagraphs 2(b) through 2(e), 3-2(b) and 4 through 
6 of paragraph (1), and paragraph (4) (the amount less than KRW 1 shall be discarded; 
the same hereinafter in [Annex 1] and [Annex 1-4]) does not match the quotation price 
unit, it shall be the price closest to that price among the prices that are higher than that 
price and match the quotation price unit. (Amended on August 26, 2005; February 3, 2009; 
January 27, 2011; September 2, 2014; December 10, 2014; February 14, 2022; April 12, 
2023; February 27, 2025)   

(4)  Notwithstanding  paragraph  (1)1,  in  cases  where  stocks  of  an  investment  company 
have not been traded from the first day of the previous month to one (1) day prior to the 
second Monday of the current month, the most recently published price of the base prices 
calculated in accordance with Article 238(6) of the Act shall be the base price applicable 
on the second Monday of that month (if the market is temporarily closed on the second 
Monday, it shall be the first trading day thereafter; the same hereinafter). (Amended on 
February 3, 2009; January 27, 2011) 

(5) Notwithstanding paragraphs (1) through (4), in the case of falling under any of the 
following subparagraphs, the Exchange may apply a different base price for each case: 
(Amended on February 3, 2009; May 12, 2014)   

1. Case where the market is reopened after being closed for an extensive period; and 

2. [Deleted on May 12, 2014] 

3. Case where the Exchange deems that the application of the base price mentioned in 
paragraphs (1) through (4) is clearly difficult because of the reasons such as no trading 
for an extended period, material changes in the details of rights, or drastic changes in 
the market conditions. 

§31. Daily Price Change Limit 

51 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
(1)  Pursuant  to  the  latter  part  of  [§20(1)]  of  the  Regulation,  in  cases  where  the  price 
obtained by adding the daily price limit to the base price does not match the quotation 
price unit, among the prices that are lower than such price and that match the quotation 
price unit, the price closest to such price shall be the upper limit price, and in cases where 
the price obtained by deducting the daily price limit from the base price does not match 
the quotation price unit, among the prices that are higher than such price and that match 
the quotation price unit, the price closest to such price shall be the lower limit price, and 
in cases where the base price is the lowest among the quotation price units, such price 
shall be the lower limit price. (Amended on February 27, 2025) 

(2) Pursuant to latter part of [§20(3)] of the Regulation, the case in which the price change 
limits can be determined differently are as follows: (Amended on October 13, 2022; April 
12, 2023) 

1. In the case where the market situation falls under any  of the following items, the 
price change limit may be set differently each time; 

(a)  Case where the market is reopened after being closed for an extensive period; 

and   

(b) Other cases where it is recognized that it is extremely inappropriate to apply the 
price change limit specified in [§20(2)] of the Regulation due to other reasons 
such as sudden change in market situation. 

2. In the case where the absolute value of the linked multiplier specified in the former 
part of [§20(2)] of the Regulation is less than 1, the multiplier shall not be multiplied 
when calculating the price change limit.   

(3) Pursuant to [§20(3)] of the Regulation, in the case of a newly-listed issue noted in 
[§30(1)2(a)], the highest price limit and the lowest price limit on the date of new listing     
shall be as follows: [April 12, 2023] 

1. In the case of the highest limit price; The price obtained by adding the price limit 
amount, which is an amount (amount less than the quotation price unit of the base price 
from the relevant amount shall be rounded down; the same hereinafter in this paragraph) 
produced by multiplying the base price by 3, to the base price. 

2. In the case of the lowest limit price: The price obtained by subtracting the price limit 
amount, which is an amount produced by multiplying the base price by 0.4, from the 
base price. 

Section 2-2. Liquidity Providing Quotations 
[December 1, 2005] 

52 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
§31-2. [Deleted on June 21, 2016] 

§31-3. Liquidity Providing Members 

(1)  Each  member  shall  notify  the  Exchange  the  name  of  staff-in-charge  of  tasks  of 
liquidity provision, after having designated the staff responsible for and in charge of the 
liquidity provision pursuant to [§20-2(2)1(b), 2(b), 2-2(c)&3(d)] of the Regulation and 
shall do the same in cases where the staff-in-charge is changed thereafter. (Amended on 
December 27, 2007; April 16, 2009; April 20, 2012; September 2, 2014) 

(2)  Pursuant  to  [§20-2(4)]  of  the  Regulation,  any  member  who  intends  to  provide  the 
liquidity  for collective investment  securities of ETFs, ETNs, and ELWs shall enter an 
agreement for the provision of liquidity with the Exchange. [August 20, 2021] (Amended 
on December 22, 2022) 

(3) Pursuant to [§20-2(4)] of the Regulation, any member who has entered an agreement 
for  provision  of  liquidity  for  ETNs  and  ELWs  shall  not  arbitrarily  stop  the  liquidity 
provision during the term of agreement, except for a case recognized by the Exchange. 
[April 20, 2012] (Amended on September 2, 2014) 

(4) The “case recognized by the Exchange” in paragraph (2) shall refer to the case where 
there exists no concern about the investor protection as the documents noted in each of 
the following subparagraphs are submitted: [April 20, 2012] (Amended on September 2, 
2014) 

1. Documents related to the termination of agreement for liquidity provision because 
of  a  justifiable  reason  according  to  the  agreement  for  liquidity  provision  for  the 
relevant ETNs or ELWs; 

2. Plans describing that the issuer of the relevant ETNs or ELWs intends to provide 
the liquidity as a liquidity provider;   

3.  Comport  letters  stating  that  the  liquidity  provider  will  not  resume  the  liquidity 
provision for ETNs or ELWs before at least three (3) years have elapsed from the time 
of terminating the agreement for liquidity provision; and   

4.  In  addition,  any  other  documents  that  the  Exchange  deems  necessary  for  the 
investor protection. 

(5)  With  respect  to  the  matters  noted  in  each  subparagraph  of  paragraph  (4),  liquidity 
providing members shall have prior consultation with the Exchange. [April 20, 2012] 

[December 1, 2005] 

§31-4. Agreement for Liquidity Provision 

(1)  The  “details  that  are  stipulated  in  the  Enforcement  Rules”  in  [§20-3(1)]  of  the 

53 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Regulation shall refer to details under each of the following subparagraphs: (Amended 
on November 27, 2008) 

1. Names of the member and the listed corporation;   

2. Matters about the quotation spread ratio that the member has to maintain during the 
regular session;   

3. Matters about the quotation quantity that the member must submit per quotation;   

4. Term of the agreement for liquidity provision;   

5. Matters about the service charges relating to liquidity provision; 

6.  In  the  case  of  including  a  clause  specifying  that,  when  the  daily  trading  volume 
resulting from the liquidity providing quotations placed by a member reaches to certain 
level,  such member is  exempted from the obligation to  place the liquidly providing 
quotations, such level. In such cases, one of the following criteria shall be satisfied:   

(a) It shall exceed 50/100 of the average daily trading volume of the previous month 
of the quotation submission day; and   

(b) It shall be at least 5/1000 of the total number of listed shares.   

6-2. In the case of including a clause that, if the member holds more than 2/100 of total 
number  of  shares  listed  for  an  issue  after  acquiring  the  shares  through  the  liquidity 
providing  quotations  it  has  placed  (based  on  the  settlement  date),  the  member  is 
exempted from the obligation to submit the liquidity providing bid quotations from the 
next trading day until the time when the ratio drops below 15/1000, such details.   

7.  The  clause  stating  that  in  conjunction  with  the  liquidity  provision,  the  securities 
related  the  laws  and  regulations  and  the  regulations  governing  the  business  of  the 
Exchange shall be observed.   

(2) When entering into an agreement for liquidity provision pursuant to [§20-3(2)] of the 
Regulation, terminating the relevant agreement thereafter, or changing the material details 
of the agreement, such facts shall be notified to the Exchange in accordance with [Annex: 
Form No. 2-3] at least 3 trading days before the relevant agreement becomes effective. 
Provided that, in the case of unavoidable circumstances where the agreement for liquidity 
provision has to be terminated without delay, the Exchange may be notified at the time 
when such circumstances occur. (Amended on March 6, 2009) 

(3) In cases where multiple members enter into an agreement for liquidity provision with 
an identical stock-listed corporation, the details specified in paragraphs (1)2 and (1)3 shall 
be the same.   

[December 1, 2005] 

54 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
§31-5. Obligation to Submit Liquidity Providing Quotations 

(1) The “quantity stipulated in the Enforcement Rules” in the latter part of [§20-4(1)] of 
the Regulation shall refer to the quantity noted in the following subparagraphs: [July 23, 
2020] 

1.  In  cases  where  the  total  number  of  listed  stocks  is  ten  (10)  million  or  less:  A 

quantity equivalent to 20/100 of the total number of listed stocks; 

2.  In cases where the total number of listed stocks is more than ten (10) million but 
less than or equal to fifty (50) million: The larger of two (2) million stocks and 
15/100 of the total number of listed stocks; 

3.  In cases where the total number of listed stocks is more than fifty (50) million but 
less than or equal to two hundred (200) million: The larger of seven point five 
(7.5) million stocks and 10/100 of the total number of listed stocks; and 

4.  In  cases  where  the  total  number  of  listed  stocks  exceeds  two  hundred  (200) 

million: Twenty (20) million stocks. 

(2)  “In  cases  where  it  is  specified  in  the  Enforcement  Rules”  in  [§20-4(5)]  of  the 
Regulation 
following 
subparagraphs:(Amended  on  May  29,  2006;  August  28,  2007;  December  27,  2007;

falling  under 

any  of 

cases 

shall 

refer 

the 

to

subparagraph of [§20-4(1)] of the Regulation. In such cases, when only offer (or bid) 
quotation has been submitted, the lower (or upper) limit price shall be deemed to be 
the best bid (or offer) quotation;   

1-2. Case where the quotation spread ratio cannot be reduced below the range stipulated 
in  each  subparagraph  of  [§20-4(1)]  of  the  Regulation  because  the  quotation  spread 
based on the best quotation price corresponds to one (1) quotation price unit;
