[Annex  1]  Guidelines  for  Calculation  of  Lowest  and  Highest  Quotation  Prices  for 

222 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Determining First Trading Price of Issues Using First Trading Price as Base Price 
(Amended on May 13, 2005; August 26, 2005; February 3, 2009; August 3, 2009; April 20, 2012; May 12, 
2014; December 10, 2014; April 22, 2016; December 28, 2018; June 23, 2020; July 23, 2020; April 12, 
2023; August 8, 2023; February 27, 2025) 

Guidelines for Calculation of Lowest and Highest Quotation Prices for 
Determining First Trading Price of Issues Using First Trading Price as Base Price 
(Pertaining to [§14(1)], [§30(1) and (3)], [§36], and [§55(3)] of the Enforcement Rules) 

1. Calculation method 

Except  those  cases  defined  otherwise,  the  lowest  and  highest  quotations  for  the 
determination of the first trading price for an issue using the first trading price as a base 
price shall be calculated in accordance with following formula.   

•  Lowest and highest quotation prices = Appraisal price according to paragraph 2 x 

Applicable rate according paragraph 3 

Note: If the appraisal price and the lowest and highest quotation prices do not match the 
quotation price unit, each price shall be the closest prices to those prices among prices 
that  are  higher  than  those  prices  and  that  match  the  quotation  price  units;  the  same 
hereinafter in this Annex 1.   

2. Appraisal price, etc. 

The appraisal price of an issue using the first trading price as a base price shall be each 
of the following subparagraphs, and for the issues falling under at least two (2) among 
subparagraphs  2(a)  through  2(e)  excluding  2(d),  the  appraisal  prices  are  calculated  by 
applying the relevant calculation method in consecutive order on the basis of respective 
effective date. In such cases, except the cases otherwise stipulated in each of the following 
subparagraphs,  the  corporations  subject  to  preparation  of  consolidated  financial 
statements pursuant to the Act on External Audit of Stock Companies shall be based on 
the consolidated financial statements and the audit reports thereon. 

A. Re-listed issues and issues with listing change (including a class of stocks) 

(1) Re-listing of stocks of the corporations established after split-off or merger after 
split-off of listed corporations and changing of the listing status of stocks of the 
surviving corporations:   

(a) When the net asset value of the re-listed issue and the issue with listing change 
at  the  time  of  split-off  decision  is  “positive”,  the  price  calculated  in 
accordance with the following formula for each issue. Provided that, in cases 
where it conducts a capital increase with consideration by the method of third 
party allocation, merger, stock swap or business/asset takeover (hereinafter 
referred to as the “capital increase with consideration by the method of third 
party allocation, etc.”) before the listing date (if the trading is suspended on 

223 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
the listing date, it shall be the day when trade suspension is lifted), and the 
number of the stocks issued with the issuing price lower than 50/100 of the 
appraisal  price  exceeds  the  number  of  stocks  before  the  relevant  capital 
increase with consideration by the method of third party allocation, etc., the 
lowest  value  among  the  quotation  price  units  shall  be  the  lowest  quotation 
price.   

• Appraisal price at the time of split-off = Sum of market capitalization per class 
of stocks of the company on the last trading day before the split-off  Split 
ratio  determined  at  the  shareholders’  meeting  /  Sum  of  shares  per  class  of 

stocks after split-off   

• Appraisal price at the time of merger after split-off = Sum of appraisal values 

determined  for  each  company  before  merger  after  split-off  (referring  to  the 

values obtained by multiplying the split ratio determined at the shareholders’ 

meeting by the market capitalization per class of stocks of the company before 

split-off on the last trading day)/ Sum of shares per class of stocks after merger 

after split-off 

• Split ratio determined at the shareholders’ meeting: The split ratio that was 

determined at the time of making decisions on the split-off or the merger after 

split-off at the shareholders’ meeting and publicly disclosed. 

                Note:   

1. Net asset value: The value calculated in accordance with the following formula 
on the basis of the statement of financial position (it does not necessarily require 
the consolidated statement of financial position) on which the calculation of the 
split ratio determined at the shareholders’ meeting on the split-off or merger after 
split-off  was  based.  In  such  case,  calculation  shall  be  based  on  the  latest 
statement  of  financial  position  submitted  to  the  Exchange  for  the  purpose  of 
listing. Provided that, in cases where, during the period from the relevant base 
date to the listing application date, an increase in the capital has resulted due to 
the paid-in capital increase, the amount of the capital increased (including the 
amount  exceeding  the  issuing  amount)  shall  be  added;  and  in  cases  where  a 
reduction in the capital has resulted, the amount of the capital reduction shall be 
subtracted; the same hereinafter in b).   

• Net asset value: Total assets - Total liabilities (to add the amount of debt-to-equity 
swap under the capital adjustments on the statement of financial position) + Value 
of treasury stocks - non-controlling interest 

                        2. Market capitalization refers to the amount obtained by multiplying the closing 
price by the total number of shares issued; the same hereinafter 

(b) In cases where the net asset value of an issue with listing change at the time of 
split-off decision is not “positive,” the price set forth in the followings for each 
issue:   

224 

 
 
 
 
1)  Issues with listing change   

The  lowest  quotation  price  shall  be  the  lowest  value  from  among  the 
quotation price units; the highest quotation price shall be the closing price 
of the last trading day before the split-off.   

2) Re-listed issues   

a)  Cases where the net asset value is positive: The net asset value per share   
(refers to the value obtained by dividing the net asset value by the number 
of shares issued as of the date of listing application; the same hereinafter 
in  this  Annex  1).  In  such  cases,  the  proviso  to  the  part  other  than  the 
calculation formula of (a) above shall apply mutatis mutandis.   

b) Cases where the net asset value is not positive: The lowest quotation price 
shall be the lowest value among the quotation price units and the highest 
quotation  price  shall  be  the  value  obtained  by  dividing  the  amount  of 
market capitalization of each class on the last trading day before the split-
off  by  the  number  of  stocks  issued  for  each  stock  type  of  the  newly 
established corporation (when such price do not match the quotation price 
unit, it shall be the closest prices to such price among prices that are higher 
than such price and that match the quotation price units). In such cases, 
the  calculation  shall  take  into  account  the  case  of  allocating  the  stocks 
other  than  those  of  the  company  before  the  split-off  to  the  newly 
established company.   

(2) Re-listing of new company incorporated by merger between listed corporations:   

            The price calculated in accordance with the following formula 

• Appraisal price = Sum of market capitalization by the class of stocks on the last 
trading day of the company before merger / Sum of shares by the class of stocks 
of the company after merger 

B. Of the stocks of investment companies, real estate investment companies, and ship 

investment companies, those falling under [§2(3)2]   

The lowest quotation price shall be the lowest value from among the quotation price 
units; the highest quotation price shall be the closing price on the trading day before 
the two (2) trading days from the record date noted in[§132(1)]. 

C. Issues that underwent reduction of paid-in capital 

(1) In the case of capital reduction without consideration for minority shareholders   

225 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The  appraisal  price  shall  be  the  amount  determined  by  multiplying  the  closing 
price of previous day by the merger or write-down ratio applicable to the minority 
shareholders. In such cases, the proviso to the part other than calculation formular 
of subparagraph A(1)(a) shall apply mutatis mutandis, and. in case there has been 
stock split-off or ex-right before listing, it shall be the amount calculated by taking 
into account such factors.   

(2) In the case of capital reduction with consideration for minority shareholders 

(a)  The  price  determined  according  to  following  formula.  In  such  cases,  the 
proviso  to  the  part  other  than  calculation  formula  of  subparagraph  A(1)(a) 
shall apply mutatis mutandis, and. in case there has been stock split-off or ex-
right before listing, it shall be the amount calculated by taking into account 
such factors. 

• Appraisal price = [(Closing price of previous day  Number of shares before 
capital reduction) – (Amount per share paid to minority shareholders  Total 
number of shares written-down)] / Number of shares after capital reduction 

            Note: In the case where there has been stock split, ex-rights, etc. before the listing, 
the  closing  price  of  previous  day  refers  to  the  price  calculated  by  taking  into 
account such factors. 

(b) If the amount produced by multiplying the appraisal price in a) above by 150% 
is less than the closing price of previous day, the closing price of previous day 
shall be the highest quotation price; and if the appraisal price is not “positive”, 
the lowest value of quotation price units shall be the and the closing price of 
previous day shall be the highest quotation price. 

(3)  In  the  case  of  capital  increase  with  consideration  by  allocation  to  third  party   

before the date of listing after the capital reduction   

(a) Notwithstanding items (1) and (2) above and paragraph 3, in cases where a 
capital increase with consideration by the method of third party allocation, 
etc.  is  conducted  before  the  date  of  listing  (referring  to  the  date  of 
supplementary listing as a result of the capital increase with consideration by 
the method of third party allocation, etc. and the date of listing change due to 
capital reduction, and including the date of release from trading suspension 
in case of an issue under trading suspension; the same hereinafter in this item) 
after capital reduction, and the number of stocks issued at the price less than 
10/100  of  the  appraisal  price  stipulated  in  items  (1)  and  (2)  exceeds  the 
number of shares before the aforesaid capital increase with consideration by 
the  method  of  third  party  allocation,  etc.,  the  appraisal  prices  shall  be  as 
follows. In such cases, the appraisal price shall be calculated on the relevant 
listing date, and in the case where there has been stock split, ex-rights, etc. 
before the listing, it shall be the amount calculated by taking into account such 
factors. 

226 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
1)  In  the  case  of  capital  reduction  without  consideration:  the  price  obtained 

through weighted calculation by the following formula   

• Appraisal price = [(Closing price of the previous day  Number of shares 
before  the  capital  reduction)  +  Sum  of  issuance  amounts  of  new  stocks 
resulting from the capital increase with consideration by the method of third 
party allocation, etc.] / Number of shares on the relevant listing date 

2) In the case of capital reduction with consideration: the price obtained through 

weighted calculation by the following formula 

•  Appraisal  price  =  [(Closing  price  of  previous  day    Number  of  shares 
before  the  capital  reduction)  +  Sum  of  issuance  amounts  of  new  stocks 
resulting from the capital increase with consideration by the method of third 
party  allocation,  etc.  –  Sum  of  payments  to  the  shareholders  for  capital 
reduction]/Number of shares on the relevant listing date 

(b) The lowest value among the quotation price units according to the appraisal 
price  in  subitem  (a)  above  shall  be  the  lowest  quotation  price,  and  when 
calculating  the  highest  quotation  price,  the  applicable  rate  shall  be  300%. 
Provided  that,  in  the  case  of  the  appraisal  price  calculated  according  to 
subitem  (a)2),  if  the  price  calculated  by  multiplying  the  relevant  appraisal 
price  by  300%  is  lower  than  the  closing  price  of  the  last  trading  day,  the 
closing price of previous day shall be the highest quotation price, and if the 
appraisal price is not “positive”, the closing price of previous day shall be the 
highest quotation price. 

    D. ETNs undergone a split or a reverse split 

The price obtained by the following formula 

• Assessment price: Closing price on the last trading day before split or reverse 
split x (1+ Indicative value change ratio) x Split or reverse split ratio 

• Indicative value change ratio: [(Indicative value on the day before the trading 
resumption / Split or reverse split ratio) – Indicative value per security calculated 
at the time of market closing on the last trading day] / Indicative value per security 
calculated at the time of market closing on the last trading day 

    E. Issue resuming trading after halt or suspension for at least thirty (30) trading days 

    The closing price of the last trading day. Provided that, in cases where stock split or 
ex-rights occur before trading resumes, it shall be the amount calculated taking into 
account  such  factor, and the proviso to the part other than calculation formula  of 
subparagraph A(1)(a) shall apply mutatis mutandis. 

227 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
3. Applicable rate 

When calculating the    and highest quotation price, the applicable rates in the followings 
shall be applied. In such cases, for the issues falling under at least two (2) among items 
2(a) through 2(e) excluding 2(d), the lowest applicable rate among the relevant applicable 
rates shall be applied.   

A.  Applicable rate for the calculation of the lowest quotation price: 50% 

B.  Applicable rate for the calculation of highest quotation price 

(1) In the case of issues undergone capital reduction or ETNs undergone a split or 

a reverse split: 150% 

  (2) Other issues: 200% 

4. In cases where the appraisal prices or the lowest and highest quotation prices calculated 
pursuant to subparagraphs 1 through 3 are deemed to be significantly unreasonable or 
the application of the relevant regulations is deemed difficult, the Exchange may set 
them differently. 

228 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
   
 
 
[Annex  1-2]  Guidelines  for  Calculation  of  the  Base  Price  for  the  Date  of  Quotation 
Placement for the Calculation of Quotation Quantity Limits 
[September 13, 2018] 

Guidelines for Calculation of the Base Price for the Date of Quotation Placement 
for the Calculation of Quotation Quantity Limits 
(Pertaining to [§14(1)3] of Enforcement Rules of KOSPI Market Business Regulation)   

1.  For the issues other than those noted in subparagraphs 2 through 4; the base prices 

calculated in accordance with [§30]. 

2.  For  the  issues  using  the  first  trading  price  as  the  base  price;  the  appraisal  prices 

determined in [Annex 1]. 

3.  For the issues scheduled to be delisted; the closing price on the date the transaction 
was  last  made.  Provided  that,  in  cases  where  an  issue  scheduled  to  be  delisted  has 
undergone ex-dividends, ex-rights, stock split or reverse stock split, the price shall be 
calculated by taking such event into account. 

4.  For ELWs, subscription warrants and subscription right certificates; the closing price 
on the date the transaction was last made.  Provided that, in cases where there is no 
closing price on the date the transaction was last made, it shall be the price under each 
of the following items: 

(a) For ELWs; the issuing prices. 

(b) For subscription warrants; the price calculated by deducting the exercise price from 
the base price for the date of quotation placement of the stocks to which the warrants 
are entitled (hereinafter referred to as the “entitled stocks”) under [§150] of the KOSPI 
Market  Listing  Regulation.  Provided that, if the  price  calculated is  not  positive, the 
base price for the date of quotation placement shall not be calculated. In such cases, 
the quotation quantity limits noted in subparagraph 3 of [§14(1)] shall apply with the 
quantity  determined  in  item  (d)  of  the  same  subparagraph.  The  same  shall  apply 
hereinafter to subscription right certificates. 

(c) For subscription right certificates; the price calculated by subtracting the issuing 
price from the base price for the date of quotation placement of the entitled stocks.

[Annex 1-4] Base Price for Trading of Initially Listed Stocks and DRs of Foreign Stocks 
[April 12, 2023] (Amended on August 8, 2023; February 27, 2025) 

Base Price for Trading of Initially Listed Stocks and DRs of Foreign Stocks 
(Pertaining to [§30(1)2] and [§55] of the Enforcement Rules) 

1. Stocks (Excluding stocks falling under paragraphs 2 and 3) 

A.  Case  of  stocks  that  have  been  offered  through  an  initial  public  offering  or  a 
secondary  distribution  after  one  (1)  year  retrospectively  from  the  date  of 

application for the preliminary listing review pursuant to the KOSPI Market Listing 

Regulation 

The  issuing  price  at  the  time  of  the  initial  public  offering  or  the  secondary 

distribution  immediately  before  the  date  of  listing  (if  there  are  two  (2)  or  more 

issuing prices at the time of the initial public offering or the secondary distribution, 

it shall be the amount obtained by dividing the total issuing amount by the relevant 

total number of shares issued ; the same hereinafter in this Annex 1-4). Provided 

that, in the case where an investment company, a real estate investment company, 

and  a  ship  investment  company  falls  under  followings,  it  shall  be  the  following 

price.   

(1) In the case where the issuing price of an investment company is lower than the 
base price calculated in accordance with Article 238(6) of the Act: The base price 

calculated in accordance with Article 238(6) of the Act. In this case, it shall be the 

base price that is the most recently announced based on the date of listing, and if 

it is announced on the day before the date of listing, it shall be limited to the base 
price announced by 17:00. 

(2) In the case where a real estate investment company or a ship investment company 
pays  money  to  minority  shareholders  after  an  initial  public  offering  or  the 

secondary  distribution  before  the  date  of  listing:  The  value  after  deducting  the 

amount paid. 

231 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
B.  In the case of stocks issued by a holding company which owns a corporation whose 
stocks are listed on the KOSPI market (including corporations listed whose stocks 

are  listed  on  the  KOSDAQ  market;  the  same  hereinafter  in  this  paragraph)  as  a 

wholly-owned  subsidiary  [referring  to  a  subsidiary  held  by  a  holding  company 

(referring to the holding company noted in each subparagraph of [§2(1)20] of the 

KOSPI  Market  Listing  Regulation;  the  same  hereinafter  in  this  Annex  1-4)  that 

owns  the  total  number  of  shares  of  the  subsidiary  through  stock  swap  or  stock 

transfer; the same hereinafter in this Annex 1-4] 

The price calculated according to the following formula. In such cases, the price of 

a  corporation  subject  to  the  preparation  of  consolidated  financial  statements  in 

accordance with the Act on External Audit of Stock Companies, etc. shall be based 

on the consolidated financial statements and the audit report, except as otherwise 
provided in the following relevant items (the same hereinafter in this Annex 1-4).   

• Base price = (Sum of market capitalization by class of stocks on the last trading 

day of a wholly-owned subsidiary which is a corporation that listed its stocks 

on the stock market before the date of listing of its holding company + Sum of 

net asset value by class of stocks of a wholly-owned subsidiary which is not a 

corporation that listed its stocks on the stock market) / Sum of shares issued by 

class of stocks as of the date of listing application 

            Note. 

1.  A wholly-owned subsidiary which is a corporation that listed its stocks on the 
stock market before the date of listing of its holding company: Limited to the 

case of the relevant stock swap or stock transfer. 

2.  Market capitalization: Amount obtained by multiplying the closing price by 

the number of shares issued. 

3.  A wholly-owned subsidiary which is not a corporation that listed its stocks on 
the  stock  market:  Limited  to  the  case  of  the  relevant  stock  swap  or  stock 

transfer, and in  the  case  of the stock swap, an unlisted holding corporation 

before the relevant stock swap shall be included. 

4.  Net asset value by class of stocks: The value obtained by distributing the net 
asset value in proportion to the number of shares issued by class of stocks. 
5.  Net  asset  value:  Total  assets  –  total  liabilities  (adding  debt-to-equity  swap 
amount in the capital adjustment account on the statement of financial position) 
+ treasury stock value – non-controlling interests 

232 

 
 
             
In this case, calculation shall be made based on the latest statement of financial 

position  submitted  to  the  Exchange  for  listing,  but  the  increased  capital 

(including paid-in capital in excess of par value) due to the capital increase 

with  consideration  conducted  for  the  period  from  the  base  date  of  the 

statement of financial position to the date of listing application shall be added, 

and if the capital is decreased, the reduced capital amount is subtracted. 

C.  Case of stocks that do not fall under subparagraphs A and B   

Net asset value per share (referring to the figure obtained by dividing the net asset 

value by the number of shares issued as of the date of listing application; the same 

hereinafter in this Annex 1-4.) 

2. Class of Stocks   

    A. Case of a class of stocks that have been offered through an initial public offering or 

a  secondary  distribution  after  one  (1)  year  retrospectively  from  the  date  of 

application for the preliminary listing review pursuant to the KOSPI Market Listing 

Regulation 

        The issuing price at the time of an initial public offering or a secondary distribution 

immediately before the date of listing. 

    B. Case of a class of stocks that have no initial public offering or secondary distribution 

noted in subparagraph A above 

        (1) In the case where the same type of a class of stocks to be listed together have 

been offered through an initial public offering or a secondary distribution noted 

on subparagraph A above: The price obtained by the simple arithmetic average 

of the base prices under subparagraph A of stocks of the relevant class. 

        (2) In the case that does not fall under item (1) above: the base price on the date of 

listing. Provided that, if the same class of stocks are listed, it shall be the price 
obtained  by  the  simple  arithmetic  average  of  the  base  prices  of  stocks  of  the 
relevant class. 

233 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
3. Foreign Stocks and DRs of Foreign Stocks 

    A. The issuing price at the time of an initial public offering or a secondary distribution 

after one (1) year retrospectively  from  the date  of application for the preliminary 

listing review pursuant to the KOSPI Market Listing Regulation. Provided that, if 

the price  (referred to  as  the “converted price” in  this subparagraph)  converted by 

applying the basic rate of exchange designated and announced in accordance with 

the  Foreign  Exchange  Transaction  Regulation  to  the  closing  price  (limited  to  the 

closing price confirmed before 17:00 on the day before the listing date) on the latest 

trading  day  on  a  foreign  stock  exchange  before  listing  is  lower  than  the  price 

obtained by multiplying the offering price at the time of an initial public offering or 
a secondary distribution to the rate specified below, it shall be converted price.   

        (1)  For  common  stocks  (including  DRs  whose  underlying  stocks  are  common 

stocks): 90%; and 

        (2) For other issues: 50% 

    B. In the case where the price of an issue newly issued pursuant to paragraph (A) has 

not been determined from the first day of the previous month to the day before the 

second  Monday  of  the  current  month,  the  base  price  may  be  recalculated  as  it  is 

considered newly listed on the second Monday of the current month. 

4. Re-listing of Delisted Company and New Company Established by Split-offs 

The price calculated according to any of subparagraphs 1 through 3 

5. In cases where the base price calculated pursuant to paragraphs 1 through 4 does not 

match the quotation price unit, it shall be the closest price to such price among prices that 

are higher than such price and match the quotation price unit, and if it is recognized that 

the base price is significantly unreasonable or the application of the relevant regulations 

is difficult, the Exchange may set them differently. 

234 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
[Annex 2] Base Prices of Ex-dividends or Ex-rights 
(Amended on August 26, 2005; August 3, 2009; April 20, 2012) 

Base Prices of Ex-dividends or Ex-rights 

1. Ex-dividends   

(a) Cases of paying dividend with the stocks whose class is the same as that of already-
listed stocks:   

• Base price of common stocks = (Closing price of cum dividend common stocks × 
Number of shares of common stocks before dividend) / (Number of shares of common 
stocks before dividend + Number of common stocks paid as dividend to shareholders 
of common stocks)   

• Base price of other type of stocks = (Closing price of cum  dividend other type of 
stocks × Number of shares of other type of stocks before dividend) / (Number of shares 
of  other  type  of  stocks  before  dividend  +  Number  of  other  type  of  shares  paid  as 
dividend to shareholders of other type of stocks)   

(b) Cases of paying dividend with either common stocks or other type of stocks to the 
already-listed common stocks and other type of stocks:   

(i) Case of paying dividend with common stocks   

• Base price of common stocks = (Closing price of cum dividend common stocks × 
Number  of  shares  of  common  stocks  before  dividend)  /  (Number  of  shares  of 
common stocks before dividend + Number of common stocks paid as dividend to 
shareholders of common stocks)   

• Base price of other type of stocks = (Closing price of cum dividend other type of 
stocks × Number of shares of other type of stocks before dividend – Base price of 
common  stocks  x  Number  of  shares  of  common  stocks  paid  as  dividend  to 
shareholders  of  other  type  of  stocks)  /  Number  of  shares  of  other  type  of  stocks 
before dividend   

(ii) Case of paying dividend with other type of stocks   

• Base price of common stocks = (Closing price of cum dividend common stocks × 
Number of shares of common stocks before dividend – Base price of other type of 

235 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
stocks x Number of other type of stocks paid as dividend to shareholders of common 
stocks) / Number of shares of common stocks before dividend   

• Base price of other type of stocks = (Closing price of cum dividend other type of 
stocks × Number of shares of other type of stocks before dividend) / (Number of 
shares of other type of stocks before dividend + Number of shares of other type of 
stocks paid as dividend to shareholders of other type of stocks)   

2. Ex-rights   

(a) Cases of allocating stocks whose class is the same as that of already-listed stocks:   

•  Base  price  of  common  stocks  =  (Closing  price  of  cum  rights  common  stocks  × 
Number of shares of common stocks before capital increase + Issuing price of common 
stocks x Number of shares of common stocks  allocated to  shareholders of common 
stocks) / (Number of shares of common stocks before capital increase + Number of 
shares of common stocks allocated to shareholders of common stocks)   

• Base price of other type of stocks = (Closing price of cum rights other type of stocks 
× Number of shares of other type of stocks before capital increase + Issuing price of 
other type of stocks x Number of shares of other type of stocks allocated to shareholders 
of  other  type  of  shares)  /  (Number  of  shares  of  other  type  of  stocks  before  capital 
increase + Number of shares of other type of stocks allocated to shareholders of other 
type of shares)   

(b) Cases of allocating either common stocks or pother type of stocks to the already-
listed common stocks and other type of stocks:   

(i) Case of allocating common stocks   

• Base price of common stocks =  (Closing  price of cum  rights  common  stocks × 
Number of common stocks before capital increase + Issuing price of common stocks 
x Number of common stocks allocated to shareholders of common stocks) / Number 
of common stocks before capital increase + Number of common stocks allocated to 
shareholders of common stocks   

• Base price of other type of stocks = [(Closing price of cum rights common stocks 
× Number of other type of stocks before capital increase + (Issuing price of common 
stocks – Base price of common stocks) x Number of common stocks allocated to 
shareholders  of  other  type  of  stocks]  /  Number  of  shares  of  other  type  of  stocks 
before capital increase   

236 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
(ii) Case of allocating other type of stocks   

• Base price of common stocks =  [Closing  price of cum  rights  common  stocks × 
Number of common stocks before capital increase + (Issuing price of other type of 
stocks  –  Base  price  of  other  type  of  stocks)  x  Number  of  other  type  of  stocks 
allocated  to  shareholders  of  common  stocks]  /  Number  of  common  stocks  before 
capital increase   

•  Base  price  of  other  type  of  stocks  =  (Closing  price  of  cum  rights  other  type  of 
stocks × Number of other type of stocks before capital increase + Issuing price of 
other type of stocks x Number of other type of stocks allocated to shareholders of 
other  type  of  stocks)  /  (Number  of  other  type  of  stocks  before  capital  increase  + 
Number of other type of stocks allocated to shareholders of other type of stocks)   

Notes: 

1. In cases of paying dividend with or allocating the stocks whose class is different from 
that of already-listed stocks, it shall be deemed that among the already-listed stocks, the 
stocks whose class is most similar to that already-listed are paid as dividend or allocated.   

2. The term "closing price of cum dividend" or "closing price of cum rights" refers to the 
closing price of one (1) day before the action date of ex-rights or ex-dividend. Provided 
that, in the case of the first ex-dividend for an initially-listed issue, the closing price of 
cum  dividend  shall  be  the  closing  price  of  an  issue  whose  trading  volume  during  the 
period until one (1) month prior to the end of the relevant listing year is the largest, from 
among the listed issues of the relevant companies; when such company is listed during 
the last month of the business year, it shall be the closing price of an issue whose trading 
volume is the largest during such month.   

3. The term “issuing price” shall be the value falling under any of the followings and the 
issuing price at the time of capital increase without consideration shall be “zero”.   

(a) Of the issuing prices (referring to the expected issuing prices or final issuing price) 
that the listed  company  published by calculating them before the  action  date of ex-
rights, the most recent price; and   

(b) In cases where no price equivalent to those noted in a) above is available, the price 
that the Exchange calculated using the following formula (in  cases  where the listed 
company has made public the formula for calculation of issuing price, such formula 
shall be used: the same hereinafter), while taking into consideration such factors as the 

237 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
base price that the listed company published most recently and discount rate. In such 
cases, in the event that the reckoning date for the calculation of base price using the 
following formula is after the action date of ex-rights, if the capital increase is carried 
out by way of “right offerings”, “3 trading days before the record date for new share 
allotment” and if the capital increase is carried out by way of “standby right offering”, 
“3  trading  days  before  the  closing  date  of  shareholder  register”  shall  be  used, 
respectively, as the reckoning date for the calculation of base price.   

Issuing price= [Base price x (1- Discount rate)] / (1 + Ratio of capital increase without 
consideration + Ratio of capital increase with consideration x Discount rate)   

4.  The  term  “number  of  stocks  paid  as  dividend  or  allocated  to  the  shareholders  of 
common  stocks  (other  type  of  stocks)  refers  the  number  of  shares  calculated  by 
multiplying the ratio of the number of common stocks (other type of stocks) to the total 
number of stock issued on the day before the action date of ex-rights or ex-dividend to 
the total number of stocks to be issued as a result of dividend or capital increase.   

238 

 
 
 
 
 
[Annex 2-2] Criteria for Liquidity Assessment and Selection of Low-liquidity Issues 
[March 25, 2016] (Amended on June 21, 2016; February 28, 2017; September 7, 2017; September 13, 2018; 
December 6, 2018; November 28, 2019; November 26, 2020; March 12, 2021; July 15, 2022) 

Criteria for Liquidity Assessment and Selection of Low-liquidity Issues, ETC 
(Pertaining to §31-12, §31-14, §31-17 and §56-3) 

1. Criteria for Liquidity Assessment   

(a)Assessment target period and issues subject to assessment 

(1)  Assessment  target  period:  From  October  of  the  year  preceding  the  year  which 
includes the selection date to September of the relevant year 

(2) Issues subject to assessment: Stocks and DRs of foreign stocks (excluding common 
stocks issued by a SPAC under Article 2(1)25 of the KOSPI Market Listing Regulation, 
the issues scheduled to be delisted, and the issues with less than 60 trading days during 
the assessment target period) 

(b)Parameters for liquidity assessment 

Parameters are calculated by arithmetically averaging the daily figures of  each of the 
following  parameters  over  the  number  of  trading  days  during  the  assessment  target 
period excluding the days of trading suspension. 

(1) Turnover ratios 

The turnover ratio is calculated based on the value obtained by dividing the volume of 
trades {limited to the volume of trades concluded during the trading hours of regular 
sessions by the methods of individual auction under [§23(1)2, 3 & 5] of the Regulation 
and  [§24]  of  the  Regulation;  the  same  hereinafter  in  this  Annex}  by  the  number  of 
listed shares.   

(2) Effective spread 

An effective spread is the spread that reflects the average executed prices during the 
trading hours of call auction in regular sessions when the market-taking quotations in 
average size of each issue during the assessment period are submitted, and calculated 
by the following formula: 

Effective spread = (Effective bid spread ÷ Quotation price unit) + (Effective offer 
spread ÷ Quotation price unit), where 

Effective bid spread = Average purchasing price – Average of the best bid and offer 
quotations, and 
Effective offer spread = Average of the best bid and offer quotations – Average selling 

239 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
price 

(3) Trading cycle 

Trading  cycle  refers  to  the  time  interval  between  executed  trades  during  regular 
sessions and it is calculated by the following formula: 

Trading cycle = Regular trading hours ÷ Number of trades(*) 

* The number of trades shall be based on the number of trades by call auctions, and in the 
case of those issues of which trading methods are stipulated differently pursuant to [§38-2] 
and [§38-3] of the Regulation, it refers to the number of trades during the trading hours of 
regular  sessions  (excluding  the  number  of  trades  executed  with  extended  scope  of 
participating quotations as a result of the change in trading methods pursuant to [§26-2] of 
the Regulation). 

2. Criteria for Selection of Market-making Target Issues, etc. 

(a) Selection criteria 

Market-making  target  issues  shall  be  the  issues  of  which  the  results  of  liquidity 
assessment  conducted  pursuant  to  subparagraph  1  satisfy  any  of  the  followings. 
Provided that issues that are newly listed or re-listed during the assessment target period 
so their number of trading days is less than 60or issues that are newly listed or re-listed 
after the assessment target period may be designated as market-making target issues by 
a method separately specified by the Exchange even if any of the following criteria is 
not met: 

  (1) An issue meeting all of the following criteria 

Assessment index 

Criteria for selection 

Turnover ratios 

Effective spreads 

Trading cycle 

Within top 50% in the order of largest volume among total 
issues subject to assessment 
Below top 50% in the order of smallest effective spreads 
among total issues subject to assessment 
Within 600 seconds (10 minutes) 

(2) An issue meeting all of the following criteria 

Assessment index 

Criteria for selection 

Turnover ratios 

Effective spreads 

Trading cycle 

Below top 50% in the order of largest volume among total 
issues subject to assessment 
Within top 50% in the order of smallest effective spreads 
among total issues subject to assessment 
Within 600 seconds (10 minutes) 

(3) An issue meeting all of the following criteria 

240 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Assessment index 

Criteria for selection 

Turnover ratios 

Effective spreads 

Trading cycle 

Within top 50% in the order of largest volume among total 
issues subject to assessment 
Within top 50% in the order of smallest effective spreads 
among total issues subject to assessment 
Within 600 seconds (10 minutes) 

(b) Exclusion criteria 

Notwithstanding item (a), any issue that falls under any of the following criteria shall be 
excluded from the list of market-making target issues: 

(1)  An  issue  with  a  liquidity  provision  agreement  in  force  as  of  the  last  day  of  the 
assessment target period;   

(2) An issue with a market capitalization of KRW ten (10) trillion or more as of the 
last trading day of the liquidity assessment target period; and 

(3) Other issues that the Exchange deems necessary to exclude from the list of market-
making target issues for the purpose of market administration. 

(c) Timing of selection 

The  selection  and  the  public  announcement  of  the  result  thereof  shall  be  made  by 
December of the year in which the end date of the assessment target period falls. 

(d) Effective period 

The selection shall be effective from January to December of the year following the year 
in which the selection date falls.   

(e) Notwithstanding item (c) and item (d), in cases where it is deemed necessary for the 
market management, the Exchange may determine the selection timing and the effective 
period for market-making target issues differently. 

3. Selection Criteria of Low Liquidity Issues subject to Call auction, etc. 

(a) Selection criteria 

The low liquidity issues subject to call auction shall be the issues of which the trading 
cycle  exceeds  600  seconds  or  10  minutes,  according  to  the  result  of  the  liquidity 
assessment conducted pursuant to subparagraph 1. 

(b) Exclusion criteria 

Notwithstanding item (a), an issue for which a liquidity provision agreement was entered 
into and put in force during the period from the assessment target period to the trading 

241 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
day immediately before the first trading day of the effective period, or an issue of which 
average trading cycle for the 3 months immediately preceding the first trading day of 
the effective period (the last trading day of the latest 3 months shall be excluded; the 
same hereinafter in this Subparagraph) is 60 seconds or shorter shall be excluded from 
the list of low liquidity issues subject to call auction.   

(c) Timing of selection 

The  selection  and  the  public  announcement  of  the  result  thereof  shall  be  made  by 
December of the year in which the end date of the assessment target period falls. 

(d) Effective period 

The selection shall be effective from January to December of the year following the year 
in which the selection date falls.   

(e) Notwithstanding items(c) and (d), in the case of an issue falling under any of the 
following cases after the effective period may be excluded from or additionally included 
to the list of low liquidity issues subject to call auction in accordance with the manner 
specified  in  each  of  such  cases.  In  such  cases,  the  effective  period  shall  be  from  the 
relevant month to the last trading day of the month in which the period under item (d) 
ends. 

(1) [Deleted on September 13, 2018] 

(2) In the case of an issue that has  entered into  a liquidity provision agreement, the 
exclusion begins from the month following the month to which the effective date of 
the agreement belongs; 

(3) In the case of an issue of which average trading cycle for the latest three (3) months 
is  sixty  (60)  seconds  or  shorter,  the  exclusion  begins  from  the  month  following  the 
month when the average trading cycle was calculated; 

(4) In the case of an issue of which liquidity provision agreement has been terminated 
or expired during the effective period after the assessment target period, the additional 
inclusion  begins  from  the  month  following  the  month  which  the  effective  date  of 
termination or the next day of the expiry date of the agreement belongs to; and 

(5) In the case of an issue of which average trading cycle for the latest three (3) months 
is  longer  than  sixty  (60)  seconds,  the  additional  inclusion  begins  from  the  month 
following the month when the average trading cycle was calculated. 

242 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
[Annex 2-3] Criteria for Selection of Market Makers and Issues for Market-making 
[March 25, 2016] (Amended on February 28, 2017; December 6, 2018; July 15, 2022) 

Criteria for Selection of Market Makers and Issues for Market-making 

1. Basic Principles 

The  Exchange  shall  select  a  market  maker  based  on  its  basic  capabilities  for  market-

making and its performance, etc.   

2. Criteria for Selection of Market-making Issues 

A selected market maker may choose the issue subject to market-making agreement in 

accordance with the following criteria: 

(a)  Priority: The priority in selecting market-making issues shall be given in descending 

order of the assessment scores on the eligibility of each market maker. 

(b) Method of selection: Each market maker sequentially picks market-making issues 
one by one below the number of issues determined by the Exchange in consideration 

of the priority stated in Subparagraph (a) and the total  number of  market-making 

issues.   

243 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
[Annex  2-4]  Guidelines  for Assessment  of  Market  Makers  and  Making  Payments  for 
Market-making 
[March 25, 2016] (Amended on February 28, 2017; September 7, 2017; December 6, 2018; December 28, 
2018; March 25, 2020; March 12, 2021; August 4, 2022) 

Guidelines for Assessment of Market Makers and Making Payments for Market-making 

I. Market-making Obligation and Assessment 

1. Assessment of fulfillment of obligations 

(a)Daily fulfillment of obligations 

In  cases  where  the  following  requirement  is  met  as  quotations  for  an  obligatory 
market-making  issue  are  submitted  during  a  day,  the  day  shall  be  counted  as  an 
“obligation-fulfilled day”(*) 

* It refers the trading day when the time period for which market-making quotations have been 
maintained at the level of both the obligatory spread and the minimum amount for quotation 
maintenance during the day takes 80% or more (referred to as the day’s ratio of submission of 
minimum  obligatory  quotations)  of  the  total  time  period  for  which  the  market-making 
obligation occurred. 

   Maintaining time of market-making quotation that 

fulfilled the obligation (in seconds) 

 Occurrence time of quotation obligation for 
obligatory issue (in seconds) 

× 100 ≧ 80% 

(1) Occurrence time of quotation obligations 

i. Occurrence time of quotation obligations: The time period from market opening 
to 15:20, excluding the following time (in seconds) 

(a) The time falling under each of the subparagraphs under [§31-17(2)]; and 

(b) In cases where an issue falls under causes for suspension or termination of 
market-making pursuant to the market-making agreement, such time period of 
suspension or termination. 

ii. Assessment period 

All the trading days when the market-making obligations have occurred. Provided 
that, if the occurrence time of quotation obligation for a day is less than one hour 
(or 3,600 seconds), such day shall be excluded from the number of market-making 
days. 

244 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
(2) Maintaining time for obligatory quotations 

i.  The  time  (in  seconds)  during  which  the  market-making  quotations  that  were 
submitted for market-making issues according to each of the subparagraphs under 
[§31-12(1)] have been maintained.

When  the  performance  of  a  market  maker  during  a  quarter  satisfies  the  following 
requirement, the relevant quarter shall be appraised as ‘obligation fulfilled’. Provided

2. Assessment on the activeness in fulfilling obligations 

The ‘activeness in fulfilling obligations’ shall be assessed for those issues that have 
been appraised as ‘obligation fulfilled’ among the market-making issues. 

Assessment score for the level of obligation fulfillment =   

 Ratio of daily obligation fulfillment + Ratio of maintenance of best quotations 

(a) Ratio of daily obligation fulfillment: 

246 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The quarterly average of obligation fulfillment ratios * that are calculated by the 
formula to examine the daily obligation fulfillment. 

* The time during which the market-making quotations fulfilling obligations (in seconds) / 
The time during which the quotation obligation for obligatory issue occurred (in seconds) 

(b) Ratio of maintaining the best quotations 

The quarterly average of the figures calculated by the following formula: 

The  time  of  a  trading  day  during  which  the  market-making  quotations  were 
maintained with the best quotations (sum of offers and bids) / The time of a trading 
day during which the market-making quotations fulfilling daily quotation obligation 
were maintained. 

II. Measures to be taken based on Assessment Results 

1. Basic principles 

(a) For the ‘obligations fulfilled,’ payments for market-making shall be made based on 

the result of assessment on the activeness in fulfilling obligations. 

(b)  The  ‘obligations  unfulfilled’  shall  be  subject  to  imposition  of  demerit  points  or 
termination of market-making agreement depending on the levels of nonfulfillment. 

2. Detailed measures 

(a) Payments for market-making for ‘fulfilled obligations’ 

* Please refer to ‘III. Payments for Market-making’ for details. 

(b) Imposition of demerit points against ‘unfulfilled obligations’ 

In  cases  when  the  number  of  days  for  which  obligations  were  fulfilled  for  each 
product during a quarter falls short of the ‘minimum number of days with fulfilled 
obligations’, the demerit points shall be imposed differentially based on the level of 
nonfulfillment. 

<Demerit points for market makers> 

Calculation methods 

Minimum number of days with fulfilled obligations – 
Number of days with fulfilled obligations per product 

Demerit points 

 Under 5 days: 1 point 
5~9days: 2 points 
10~19 days: 3 points 
20~29 days: 4 points 
 Over 30 days: 5points 

(c) Suspension of qualification based on accumulated demerit points

When the suspension of qualification takes effect the period set forth in [§31-21(2)],

III. Payments for Market-making   

1. Prerequisite for payment for market-making 

Fee revenue is shared among the market-making issues for which market-making 
obligation was fulfilled; and   

  The  calculation  of  the  share  of  fee  revenue  shall  be  made  for  the  issues  that  are 
assessed as ‘obligation fulfilled’ (‘issues subject to payment’) among market-making 
issues. 

2. Calculation of amounts to be allocated 

Amount of fee revenue allocation 
= ∑ (Fee revenue from ‘issues subject to payment’ × A market maker’s share of trading 
volume of ‘issues subject to payment’ ×  Payment ratio based on the activeness in 
fulfilling obligations) 

(a) Fee revenue from ‘issues subject to payment’ 

The fee revenue of the Exchange earned from the issues subject to payment, which 
is the sum of trading fees and clearing fees. 

(b) Trading share of ‘issues subject to payment’ 

Trading share of issues 
subject to payment (%) 

=   

ⓑA market maker’s trading volume of issues subject to 
payment during a quarter 

248 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
ⓐTrading volume of issues subject to payment during a 
quarter 

(1) Trading volume of issues subject to payment during a quarter 

Total trading volume of issues subject to payment during a quarter; 
Sum of purchasing and selling trading volumes; and 
Block trading, basket trading, competitive block trading and after-hours trading 
shall be included. 

(2) Market maker’s trading volume of issues subject to payment during a quarter 

The trading volume that has been executed by a market maker out of accumulated 
trading volume of an issue subject to payment during a quarter; and 

The trades which are not exempted from trading fees such as the cross transactions, 
the trading by other quotations to offset a long position and the trading volume by 
the immediately executing quotations shall be excluded. 

(c) Payment rates based on the activeness in fulfilling obligations 

The  payment  rates  are  determined  by  dividing  the  assessment  scores  on  the 
activeness in fulfilling obligations for the issues subject to payment by “200”. 

(d) Payment of fixed amount of compensation 

In cases where the market-making issues are assessed as ‘obligation fulfilled’, the 
amounts pre-determined in the market-making agreement may be paid to the issues 
specified in the agreement. 

3. Timing of payments 

Payments  shall  be  made  within  three  (3)  months  after  the  end  of  each  quarter. 
Provided that, when the Exchange deems it necessary due to changes in the contents 
of market-making agreements, the timing of payment may be determined differently.   

IV. Criteria to Terminate Market-making Agreement 

An issue whose average daily turnover rate (excluding the last 7 trading days of each 
quarter)  calculated  based  on  formula  in  item  1  below  exceeds  the  ratio  of  B  for  2 
consecutive quarters. 

1.  Turnover ratio 

249 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The ratio calculated according to the following formula based on the trading date of 
the issue concerned. 

Turnover ratio (%) 

=   

Trading volume 

Number of listed shares 

* Limited to the volume of transactions executed by the method of continuous auction 

referred to in [§23(1)2,3 and5] and [§24] of the Regulation   

2.  Rate: 15%

[Annex 2-5] Assessment Method for Designation of LPB Dealer and Designation Method

Assessment of LPB Dealers 

1. Assessment period 

(a)  First  half  assessment:  From  December  of  the  previous  year  to  May  of  the  year 
(provided that the assessment period of new members admitted for the year shall 
be from January to May). 

    (b) Second half assessment: From June to November of the year   

2. Assessment items and scores

Note.  In  the  table  above,  “sales  entrustment  contract  member”  shall  refer  to  a  member  who  has 
entered into a sales contract with a sales agency pursuant to [§95] of the Regulation. 

3. Assessment method per item 

    (a) Submission of reported price 

(1) Reported price 

In  cases  where  a  price  reported  by  the  LPB  dealer  (hereinafter  referred  to  as  the 
“reported  price”)  noted in [§74(3)] has  failed to  be  submitted, 0.5  points shall be 
deducted for each case.   

(2) Disparate ratio from the reported market yield 

251 

 
 
 
 
 
 
     
   
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
First, for all LPB dealers, the daily average of the absolute value of the difference 
between the reported yield (referring to the rate of return converted by applying the 
method specified in each subparagraph of [§16] to the reported price) and the mark-
to-market  yield  (referring  to  the  rate  of  return  converted  by  applying  the  method 
specified in each subparagraph of [§16] to the mark-to-market price noted in [§65(2)] 
of the Regulations; the same hereinafter) during the assessment period for each bond 
type is multiplied by the proportion of the issuance volume of the relevant bond type 
among  the  issuance  volume  of  all  bond  type  during  the  same  period,  and  the 
combined value is then used to determine the ranking in ascending order. Next, all 
LPB dealers shall be divided into six (6) tiers [the number of LPB dealers in tiers 1 
through 5 is the total number of LPB dealers divided by 6  (rounding up at the 1st 
decimal place), and the number of remaining LPB dealers shall be the number of 
LPB dealers in tier 6; the same hereinafter] according to the ranking of the combined 
value, and then the full score shall be assigned to the LPB dealers in the first tier and 
then  the  assessment  score  shall  be  assigned  sequentially  to  the  LPB  dealers 
belonging to  the next lowest  tier by deducting  one point five (1.5) points each in 
ascending order. 

(3) Submission of obligatory bid quotations 

In cases where an LPB dealer violates (classifying the time period before the market 
opening and the time period during the last twenty (20) minutes before the market 
closing  time  each  day)  [§74(1)  or  (2)],  point  five  (0.5)  points  per  case  shall  be 
deducted. Provided that, in cases where the violation occurs on any of the following 
days  during  the  assessment  period,  an  additional  one  (1)  point  per  case  shall  be 
deducted for each violation:   

            (i) A day when the opening price falls below the offer price pursuant to [§76(5)]; 

or 

            (ii) A day when  the price immediately before the  closing price falls below the 

reported market price. 

(4) Quantity of obligatory bid quotations 

First,  for  all  LPB  dealers,  the  quantity  of  obligatory  bid  quotations  submitted 
pursuant to [§74(1) and (2)] for bonds issued in the current month (on the first day 
of  each  month,  it  shall  be  the  bonds  issued  in  the  previous  month)  on  all  of  the 
following days [the day in (iii) shall be limited to bond under [§61(1)] during the 
assessment period shall be calculated for each bond type. Next, all LPB dealers shall 
be  divided  into  six  (6)  tiers  according  to  the  ranking  of  the  combined  values  in 
descending order, and then the full score shall be assigned to the LPB dealers in the 
first tier and the assessment score shall be assigned sequentially to the LPB dealers 
belonging  to  the  next  highest  tier  by  deducting  one  (1)  point  each  in  descending 
order: 

    (i) A day when the mark-to-market yield pursuant to [§65(2)] of the Regulation 

252 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
declined to the coupon rate or below; 

    (ii) The next business day of the holiday when sales occurred 

    (iii) The day when the bond yield in the followings rises above the reported yield 
(referring to the yield calculated by converting the reported price pursuant to 
[§53(2)] of the Regulations into the yield calculated by applying the methods 
specified in each subparagraph of [§16]: 

          ⓐ  Before market opening: The mark-to-market yield on the day; and 

          ⓑ  From 20 minutes before market closing: The yield immediately before the 

closing price of the day. 

(5) Trading performance of LPBs   

First,  for  all  LPB  dealers,  the  average  daily  trading  volume  shall  be  shall  be 
calculated for each bond type. Next, all LPB dealers shall be divided into six (6) tiers 
according to the ranking of the combined values in descending order, and then the 
full score shall be assigned to the LPB dealers in the first tier and the assessment 
score shall be assigned sequentially to the LPB dealers belonging to the next highest 
tier by deducting three point five (3.5) points each in descending order. In this case, 
the trading volume in the followings is excluded, and if the daily trading volume of 
a bond, for each bond type, exceeds three (3) times the average daily trading volume 
of the bond in the previous month, the trading volume of the relevant bond on that 
day is excluded: 

    (i) Self-account transactions where the same LPB dealer has placed both the bid 

and offer quotations;   

(ii) Selling transactions conducted according to the sales agent contract; 

(iii) Customer account transactions; and 

(iv)  Offset  transactions  that  offset  original  position  (transactions  where  after   
executing  a  trade,  the  member  who  previously  sold  buys  and  changes 
position,  while  the  member  who  previously  bought  sells  and  changes 
position, each at the same price and quantity with those of the previous trade 
during the same trading day). 

(6) Market-making performance in LPB market 

First,  all LPB dealers shall be ranked based on their market-making performance 
points, which are assigned after an assessment conducted by applying the assessment 
methods in annex 4 mutatis mutandis during the assessment period and divided into 
six (6) tiers according to the ranking of the performance points in descending order. 
Next,  the  full  score  shall  be  assigned  to  the  LPB  dealers  in  the  first  tier  and  the 

253 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
assessment score shall be assigned sequentially to the LPB dealers belonging to the 
next highest tier by deducting one (1) point each in descending order. 

(7) Submission of offer quotations for bonds under sales agent contract 

In cases where an LPB dealer violates [§76(5)] and the latter part of [§124(2)], point 
five (0.5) points per case shall be deducted.   

(8) Government policy cooperation 

Additional points shall be awarded if any of the following applies: 

            (i) Performance of duties as Chairperson or Secretary of the LPB Dealers Council:   

Three (3) points; 

            (ii)  Performance  of  duties  as  Vice  Chairperson  or  Auditor  of  the  LPB  Dealers 

Council: One (1) points; and 

        (iii)  Contribution  to  policy  coordination,  including  participation  in  regulatory 

reform: Up to two (2) points. 

254 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
[Annex 2-6] Method for Designation of Market-making STRIP Bond Issue 
[October 29, 2024] 

Method for Designation of Market-making STRIP Bond Issue 
(Pertaining to [§79-2(1)] and [§99-5(1)c]) 

1.  The  designation  dates  for  STRIP  bond  issues  subject  to  market-making  quotation 
submission  (hereinafter  referred  to  as  the  “market-making  target  issue”)  shall  be 
February  15,  May  15,  August  15,  and  November  15  of  each  year.  However,  if  the 
relevant date is a market holiday or a business day immediately preceding the due date 
for  holding  reserve  set  by  the  Bank  of  Korea,  the  next  trading  day  shall  be  the 
designation date. If necessary for market management, taking into consideration the 
listing status and repayment schedule of the STRIP bonds, the designation date may be 
changed. 

2. The Exchange shall designate and announce a market-making target issue on the last 
trading  day  of  the  month  preceding  the  month  in  which  the  designation  date  falls 
(hereinafter referred to as the “designation notice date”). 

3. A market-making target issue shall be a STRIP bond noted in Article 2, Paragraph 10 
of the Regulation on Operation of Treasury Bonds and the maturity date of the market-
making target issue shall be one of the three maturity dates nearest to the designation 
date (excluding cases where the maturity date is within one month from the designation 
date). 

4. The submission period of market-making quotations for the market-making target issue 
shall be 9 months from the designation date. However, the submission period for the 
market-making quotations may be set differently in consideration of the designation 
date in subparagraph 1. 

5. When designating a new market-making target issue, the Exchange shall designate one 
(1)  issue  as  the  market-making  target  issue  in  the  following  order  based  on  the 
designation notice date. However, if there is no balance of listed amount of the relevant 
issue 3 business days before the designation date, the market-making target issue may 
be redesignated in the following order based on 3 business days before the designation 
date: 

    A. Principal strips with a large listed balance; 

B. Principal strips of which original coupon bond has a short maturity; and 

    C. STRIP bonds determined by the Exchange taking into consideration of the listed 

balance, trading volume, etc. of the original coupon bonds. 

255 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
6. If necessary for market management, the Exchange may designate an interest strip as 
a market-making target  issue noted in  Article 2,  Paragraph 11 of  the  Regulation  on 
Operation of Treasury Bonds. In this case, subparagraphs 1, 3, and 4 shall apply mutatis 
mutandis to the designation date, the maturity date of the market-making target issue, 
the submission period of market-making quotations, etc. 

7. If necessary for market management, the Exchange may change the maturity date of a 
market-making  target  issue  despite  the  provisions  of  subparagraph  3  or  change  the 
market-making target issue by maturity date in consideration of market liquidity, etc. 
In this case, the submission period for the market-making quotation in subparagraph 4 
shall be determined separately by the Exchange.

257 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
[Annex  4]  Methods  for Assessment  of  Market-making  Performance  of  Bond  Market-
making Members 
(Amended  on  December  31,  2009;  July  1,  2010;  March  23,  2011;  February  28,  2014;  July  16,  2015; 
November 9, 2015; March 24, 2016; June 21, 2016; December 26, 2016; June 9, 2017; August 24, 2017; 
September  13,  2018;  May  26,  2020;  May  28,  2020;  June  8,  2021;  October  29,  2024;  March  25,  2025; 
December 24, 2025) 

Methods for Assessment of Market-making Performance of 
Bond Market-making Members 

1. Basic Market-making Requirements for Bond Market-making Members 

(a) Basic Number of Issues subject to Market-making 

(1) For the trading in the KRX KTB: six (6) or more issues. Provided that, among the 
6  issues,  3  or  more  shall  be  benchmark  issues  and  STRIPS  shall  be  excluded  in 
calculating the 6 issues.) 

(2) For the trading in the KRX LPB: one (1) or more issues per bid or offer and per 
class* of bonds (in cases where all or part of the bonds in a class are not issued, the 
relevant class may be excluded.), and four (4) or more issues in total. 

* The classes of LPBs include Type I National Housing Bonds, Seoul Railroad Bonds, 
Regional Development Bonds and Metropolitan Railroad Bonds specified in [§74(1)]. 

(3) For the trading in the KRX BondsAll*: fifteen (15) issues or more regardless of 
bond types 

* Referring to the trading of bonds specified in [§71-3(2)4] of the Regulation (the same 
hereinafter in this Annex). 

(b) Basic Market-Making Time 

(1) For trading in the KRX KTB 

(a) In the morning: For two and half hours during 9:00 am~12:00 noon. Provided 
that,  it  shall  be  for  one  and  half  hours  during  9:00  am  ~  12:00  noon  for  20-year 
treasury bonds and for one hour during 9:00 am ~ 12:00 noon for STRIPS. (Amended 
on March 25, 2025) 

(b) In the afternoon: For one and half hours during 1:00 pm ~3:00 pm (hereinafter 
referred  to  as  “Afternoon  I”)  and  full  time  from  3:00  pm  to  3:30  pm  (hereinafter 
referred to as “Afternoon II”). Provided that, it shall be for one hour during 1:00 pm 
~ 3:00 pm and Afternoon II for 20-year treasury bonds, for two hours during 1:00 
pm ~ 3:30 pm for 30-year treasury bonds, and for one hour during 1:00 pm ~3:30 pm 

258 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
for STRIPS. (Amended on March 25, 2025) 

* If the time period of market-making for any of the morning and afternoon of a day 
is longer than 80% of the basic market-making time, the market-making time of the 
day shall be acknowledged in full, but if the time period of market-making time for 
both of the morning and afternoon is less than 80% of the basic market-making time, 
the market-making time of the day shall not be acknowledged at all. In such cases, 
the time to be acknowledged shall be limited to the range of the basic market-making 
time (referring to the respective basic market-making time, if divided into Afternoon 
I and II).   

(2) For trading in the KRX LPB: For 2/3 of the regular trading hours (9:00 am ~3:10 
pm) 

(3) For trading in the KRX BondsAll: For 2/3 of the regular trading hours (9:00 am ~ 
3:30 pm) 

(c) Basic Number of Days for Market-making 

(1) For trading in the KRX KTB: For 80/100 or more of the total trading days during 
the period for assessment. 

(2) For trading in the KRX LPB: For at least 2/3 of the total trading days during the 
period for assessment. 

(3) For trading in other bond markets: For at least 2/3 of the total trading days during 
the period for assessment. 

*  In  calculating  the  basic  number  of  market-making  days,  the  figures  in  the  first 
decimal place shall be rounded off. 

(d)  Basic  Market-making  Score=  Basic  number  of  market-making  issues  per 
market Basic number of market-making days

(c)  For trading in KRX BondsAll 

  The  performance  in  submission  of  market-making  quotations  and  the 
performance of trading by market-making quotations shall be assessed. 

 The scores for each assessment item are as follows: 

Assessment items 
Performance of submission of market-making quotations 
Performance of trading by market-making quotations 

Scores 
30 
70 

(b) Assessment of Performance in Submission of Market-Making Quotations 

(1) Weighting criteria 

(a) For trading in KRX KTB and KRX LPB 

A weight of 1.5 times shall be granted to the cases where all of the basic market-
making requirements are met throughout the assessment period. 

(b) For trading in KRX BondsAll 

A weight of 1.5 times shall be granted to the cases where all of the basic market-
making requirements are met throughout the assessment period (“basic weight”). 

A weight of 1.5 times shall be granted to  corporate bonds  and  the special  bond 

260 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
issues such as mortgage-backed securities throughout the assessment period (“issue 
weight”). 

A  weight  of  3.0  times  shall  be  granted  to  the  number  of  issues  of  ‘low-rated 
corporate  bonds’*the  markets  for  which  were  made  throughout  the  assessment 
period (“risk weight 1”). 

* Referring to the corporate bonds specified in item (b) of [§99-6(1)4]. 

In cases where the number of corporate bonds the markets for which were made 
throughout the assessment period on a daily basis is five (5) or more, a weight of 
2.0 times shall be granted to the total number of such corporate bonds (“risk weight 
2”). 

(2) Assessment of performance in submission of market-making quotations 

For the trading in the KRX KTB: The aggregate market-making time for the issues 
that has met the basic market-making time on a daily basis (limited to trading days 
that meet both the requirement of the basic number of market-making issues and 
the requirement of the basic market-making time) during the assessment period* 
Weight 

*Calculation  of  market-making  time:  The  time  during  which  market-making 
quotations  were  maintained  /  the  total  time  during  which  market  makers  are 
obliged  to  place  market-making  quotations.  (For  20-  and  30-year  benchmark 
issues, the scores are weighted by 1.5 times). 

For  the  trading  in  the  KRX  LPB:  The  total  number  of  issues  of  which  the 
requirement of market-making time on a daily basis during the assessment period 
is met Weight 

For  the  trading  in  the  KRX  BondsAll:  The  number  of  issues  of  which  the 
requirement of market-making time on a daily basis during the assessment period 
is met Issue weight Risk weight 1 The sum of calculated Risk weight 2 on a 
daily basis Basic weight 

(3) Assessment scores for performance of submission of market-making quotations 

(a)   For trading in the KRX KTB   

 Weight of submission  performance of market-making quotations*  Assessed 

item score (20 points)   

* Weight = Performance of market-making quotations submission of a member 
/Aggregate  performance  of  market-making  quotations  submission  of  all 
market-making members)

(b) For trading in KRX LPB 

 Weight of submission  performance of market-making quotations*  Assessed 

item score (30 points)   

* Weight = Performance of market-making quotations submission of a member 
/Aggregate  performance  of  market-making  quotations  submission  of  all 
market-making members)

(c) Assessment of Performance of Trading by Market-Making Quotations 

(1) Weighting criteria 

(a) For trading in KRX KTB   

 5-year and 10-year KTBs (excluding inflation-linked KTBs): 1.5 times 

 20-year, 30-year, and 50-year KTBs, inflation-linked KTBs, and STRIPS: 
2 times 

(b) For trading in KRX LPB 

 Not applicable 

(c) For trading in KRX BondsAll 

 A weight of 1.5 times shall be granted to the non-market-making quotations that 
are  executed  with  market-making  quotations  of  a  member  throughout  the 
assessment period. 

(2) Performance of trading by market-making quotations 

 All trades matched with the market-making quotations that were submitted by 
the relevant member during the assessment periodWeight (Provided that the 
trades  of  which  corresponding  quotations  are  the  market-making  quotations 
submitted by the same member shall be excluded.) 

 In the case of KRX KTB, the performance of Repo trading for treasury bonds, 

262 

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
monetary  stabilization  bonds,  and  foreign  exchange  stabilization  fund  bonds 
during the assessment period, of which term is 2-day or longer shall be added. In 
such  cases,  the  Repo  trades  by  negotiated  and  reported  trading  (excluding  the 
reported trades under subparagraphs 5 and 6 of [§76(1)]) shall be included. 

 In the case of KRX KTB, the performance of trading executed by market-making 
quotations  submitted  through  the  bond  market-making  account  noted  in  [§99-
9(5)]  shall  be  separately  added  as  the  trading  performance  by  market-making 
quotations. 

 In case of LPB market, offset transactions*(including initial transaction) during 
the assessment period shall be excluded from the trading record.   

*  Transactions  where  after  executing  a  trade,  the  member  who  previously  sold, 
changes position and buys while the member who previously bought, changes 
position and sells, each at the same price and quantity of the previous trade during 
the same trading day.   

(3) Assessment scores for performance of trading by market-making quotations 

 Weight of submission performance of market-making quotations* Assessed 
item score (70 points)   

* Weight = Performance of trading by market-making quotations of a member / 
Aggregate performance of trading by market-making quotations of all market-
making members) 

(d) Assessment of Validity of Market-making Quotations   

(limited to the KRX KTB) 

(1) Number of issues traded by market-making quotations 

 The sum of the number of market-making quotations submitted by the relevant 
member during the assessment period. However, correction quotations to market-
making quotations shall be excluded. 

(2) Number of valid market-making quotations 

  The  sum  of  the  number  of  quotations  with  the  weights  in  the  following  table 
applied to each time period during which the buy or sell balance after the initial

member  during  the  assessment  period.  In  this  case,  if  a  correction  quotation  is 
submitted  for  the  market-making  quotation,  the  balance  of  the  initial  market-
making quotation that is the subject of the correction quotation is considered to 
be maintained.
